<p><b>FC Spartak Moscow</b> (Russian: <span lang="ru">Футбольный клуб «Спартак» Москва</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Russian" title="Help:IPA for Russian">[spɐrˈtak mɐˈskva]</a></span>) is a Russian <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club from <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>. Having won 12 <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Top_League" title="Soviet Top League">Soviet championships</a> (second only to <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv" title="FC Dynamo Kyiv">Dynamo Kyiv</a>) and nine <a href="/wiki/Russian_Premier_League" title="Russian Premier League" class="mw-redirect">Russian championships</a>, they are one of the country's most successful clubs. They have also won the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Cup" title="Soviet Cup">Soviet Cup</a> ten times and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Cup_(football)" title="Russian Cup (football)">Russian Cup</a> three times. Spartak have also reached the semi-finals of all three <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">European club competitions</a>.</p>
<p>Historically, the club was a part of the <a href="/wiki/Spartak_(sports_society)" title="Spartak (sports society)">Spartak sports society</a>. Other teams in the society include <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> club <a href="/wiki/HC_Spartak_Moscow" title="HC Spartak Moscow">HC Spartak Moscow</a>. Currently, the club is not connected with Spartak sports society and is an independent privately owned organization. They are nicknamed "Meat" (Russian: "мясо", "myaso").</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Spartak_Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation">Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Spartak_Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/FC_Presnya_Moscow" title="FC Presnya Moscow" class="mw-redirect">FC Presnya Moscow</a></div>
<p>In the early days of Soviet football, many government agencies such as the police, army and railroads created their own <a href="/wiki/Football_team" title="Football team">clubs</a>. So many statesmen saw in the wins of their teams the superiority over the opponents patronizing other teams. Almost all the teams had such kind of patrons— <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Moscow" title="FC Dynamo Moscow">Dinamo</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Militsiya" title="Militsiya">police</a>, <a href="/wiki/PFC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PFC CSKA Moscow">CSKA</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">army</a> and Spartak, created by a trade union public organization considered to be "the people's team."</p>
<p>In 1922, the Moscow Sport Circle (Moscow sport club of Krasnopresnensky district) (<span lang="ru">МКС, Московский кружок спорта</span>), later named Krasnaya Presnya, was formed by Ivan Artemyev and involved <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Starostin" title="Nikolai Starostin">Nikolai Starostin</a>, especially in its football team. The team grew, building a stadium, supporting itself from ticket sales and playing matches across the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian SFSR</a>. As part of a 1926 reorganization of football in the Soviet Union, Starostin arranged for the club to be sponsored by the food workers union and the club moved to the 13,000 seat <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Tomsky" title="Mikhail Tomsky">Tomsky</a> <a href="/wiki/Young_Pioneers_Stadium" title="Young Pioneers Stadium">Stadium</a>, known as Pishcheviki. The team changed sponsors repeatedly over the following years as it competed with Dinamo Moscow, whose 35,000 seat <a href="/wiki/Dynamo_Stadium_(Moscow)" title="Dynamo Stadium (Moscow)" class="mw-redirect">Dinamo Stadium</a> lay close by.</p>
<p>As a high-profile sportsman, Starostin came into close contact with Alexander Kosarev, secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Komsomol" title="Komsomol">Komsomol</a> (Communist Union of Youth) who already had a strong influence on sport and wanted to extend it. In November 1934, with funding from Promkooperatsiia, Kosarev employed Starostin and his brothers to develop his team to make it more powerful. Again the team changed its name, this time to <b>Spartak Moscow</b>.</p>
<p>The club founders, four Starostin brothers, played a big role in the formation of the team. The Starostins played for the red-whites in the 1930s but right before <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> they were subjected to <a href="/wiki/Political_repression" title="Political repression">repression</a> as the leaders of the most hated<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2011)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> team by the state authorities. Elder brother Nikolai Starostin wrote in his books that he had survived in the State Prison System due to his participation in football and with Spartak. After the <a href="/wiki/Rehabilitation_(Soviet)" title="Rehabilitation (Soviet)">political rehabilitation</a>, in 1954, he would later return to the team as the squad's manager.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_period">Soviet period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Spartak_Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Soviet period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1935, Starostin proposed the name Spartak that was derived from <a href="/wiki/Spartacus" title="Spartacus">Spartacus</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Gladiator" title="Gladiator">gladiator</a>-slave who led a rebellion against <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Rome</a>, and was inspired by eponymous book by Raffaello Giovagnoli. Starostin is also credited with the creation of the Spartak logo.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> The same year, the club became a part of newly-created <a href="/wiki/Spartak_(sports_society)" title="Spartak (sports society)">Spartak sports society</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spartak_Society_logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/75/Spartak_Society_logo.png/100px-Spartak_Society_logo.png" width="100" height="57" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/75/Spartak_Society_logo.png/150px-Spartak_Society_logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/75/Spartak_Society_logo.png/200px-Spartak_Society_logo.png 2x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="181" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spartak_Society_logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Spartak's third logo, still in use by <a href="/wiki/Spartak_(sports_society)" title="Spartak (sports society)">the sports society</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovak</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Antonin_Fivebr" title="Antonin Fivebr" class="mw-redirect">Antonin Fivebr</a> is credited as the first head coach of Spartak, though he worked as a consultant in several clubs simultaneously.<sup id="cite_ref-History1936_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History1936-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1936, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Top_League" title="Soviet Top League">Soviet Top League</a> was established, where its first championship was won by Dynamo Moscow while Spartak won its second, which was held in the same calendar year. Before World War II, Spartak earned two more titles.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1937 Spartak won the football tournament of <a href="/wiki/1937_Workers%27_Summer_Olympiad" title="1937 Workers' Summer Olympiad">Workers' Olympiad</a> at <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>.</p>
<p>During the 1950s, Spartak, together with Dynamo, dominated the Soviet Top League. When the <a href="/wiki/USSR_national_football_team" title="USSR national football team" class="mw-redirect">Soviet national team</a> won gold medals at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1956_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1956 Summer Olympics">Melbourne Olympics</a>, it consisted largely of Spartak players. Spartak captain <a href="/wiki/Igor_Netto" title="Igor Netto">Igor Netto</a> was the captain of the national team from 1954 to 1963. In the 1960s, Spartak won two league titles, but by the mid-1960s, Spartak was no more regarded as a leading Soviet club. The club was even less successful in the 1970s and in 1976 Spartak was relegated into the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_First_League" title="Soviet First League">lower league</a>.</p>
<p>During the following season, the stadium was still full as the club's fans stayed with the team during its time in the lower division. <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Beskov" title="Konstantin Beskov">Konstantin Beskov</a>, who became the head coach (ironically, as a footballer Beskov made his name playing for Spartak's main rivals, Dynamo), introduced several young players, including <a href="/wiki/Rinat_Dasayev" title="Rinat Dasayev">Rinat Dasayev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Yartsev" title="Georgi Yartsev">Georgi Yartsev</a>. Spartak came back the next year and won the title in 1979, beating <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv" title="FC Dynamo Kyiv">Dynamo Kyiv</a> and thanks to Spartak supporters, the period is considered to be the start of the modern-style fans' movement in the Soviet Union.</p>
<p>On 20 October 1982, <a href="/wiki/Luzhniki_disaster" title="Luzhniki disaster">disaster struck</a> during the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a> match between Spartak and Dutch club <a href="/wiki/HFC_Haarlem" title="HFC Haarlem">HFC Haarlem</a>. Sixty-six people died in a <a href="/wiki/Stampede" title="Stampede">stampede</a> during the match,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> making it Russia's worst sporting disaster.</p>
<p>In 1989, Spartak won the its last USSR Championship, rivals Dynamo Kyiv 2–1 in the closing round. Spartak's striker <a href="/wiki/Valeri_Shmarov_(footballer)" title="Valeri Shmarov (footballer)">Valery Shmarov</a> scored the "golden" <a href="/wiki/Direct_free_kick" title="Direct free kick">free kick</a> with almost no time left. The next season, Spartak reached the <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_European_Cup" title="1990–91 European Cup">European Cup</a> semi-final, consequently eliminating <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">Napoli</a> on penalties and <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> (with 3–1 away victory), but losing to <a href="/wiki/Olympique_de_Marseille" title="Olympique de Marseille">Marseille</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_period">Modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Spartak_Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:217px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Match_veteranov_Spartaka_(8).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Match_veteranov_Spartaka_%288%29.jpg/215px-Match_veteranov_Spartaka_%288%29.jpg" width="215" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Match_veteranov_Spartaka_%288%29.jpg/323px-Match_veteranov_Spartaka_%288%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Match_veteranov_Spartaka_%288%29.jpg/430px-Match_veteranov_Spartaka_%288%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="799" data-file-height="440" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Match_veteranov_Spartaka_(8).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of the <a href="/wiki/Otkrytie_Arena" title="Otkrytie Arena" class="mw-redirect">Otkrytie Arena</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Ambox_current_red.svg" class="image"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This article is <b>outdated</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please update this section to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(November 2010)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A new page in the club’s history began when the Soviet Union collapsed and its championship ceased to exist. In the newly-created Russian league, Spartak, led by coach and president <a href="/wiki/Oleg_Romantsev" title="Oleg Romantsev">Oleg Romantsev</a>, dominated and won all but one title between 1992 and 2001. Year-after-year the team also represented Russia in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>.</p>
<p>Problems began in the new century, however. Several charismatic players (<a href="/wiki/Ilya_Tsymbalar" title="Ilya Tsymbalar">Ilya Tsymbalar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrey_Tikhonov" title="Andrey Tikhonov">Andrey Tikhonov</a> among others) left the club as a result of conflict with Romantsev. Later, Romantsev sold his stock to oil magnate Andrei Chervichenko, who in 2003 became the club president. The two were soon embroiled in a row that would continue until Romantsev was sacked in 2003 with the club suffering several sub-par seasons until Chervichenko finally sold his stock in 2004. The new ownership made a number of front office changes with the aim of returning the team to the top of the Russian Premier League.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2005_in_Russian_football" title="2005 in Russian football">2005 season</a>, Spartak, led by <a href="/wiki/Aleksandrs_Starkovs" title="Aleksandrs Starkovs">Aleksandrs Starkovs</a>, finished second in the league following an impressive run to beat <a href="/wiki/FC_Lokomotiv_Moscow" title="FC Lokomotiv Moscow">Lokomotiv Moscow</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Zenit_Saint_Petersburg" title="FC Zenit Saint Petersburg">Zenit Saint Petersburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Rubin_Kazan" title="FC Rubin Kazan">Rubin Kazan</a> to the last Champions League place.</p>
<p>Following a mixed start to the 2006 season and public criticism from <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Alenichev" title="Dmitry Alenichev" class="mw-redirect">Dmitry Alenichev</a>, the team's captain and one of its most experienced players, the Starkovs left his position to <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Fedotov" title="Vladimir Fedotov">Vladimir Fedotov</a>.</p>
<p>Spartak has been entitled to place a golden star on its badge since 2003 to commemorate winning five Russian championships in 1992, 1993, 1994, 1996 and 1997. They have won the championship another four times since 1997. Since 2013, the club have added another three stars as rules allowed teams to include titles won during the Soviet era.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nickname">Nickname</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Spartak_Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Nickname">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The team is usually called "red-and-whites," but among the fans "The Meat" (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: "Мясо", "Myaso") is a very popular nickname. The origins of the nickname belong to the days of the foundation of the club; in the 1920s, the team was renamed several times, from "Moscow Sports Club" to "Red Presnya" (after the name of one of the districts of Moscow) to "Pishcheviki" ("Food industry workers") to "Promkooperatsiya" ("Industrial cooperation") and finally to "Spartak Moscow" in 1935, and for many years the team was under patronage of one of the Moscow food factories that dealt with meat products.</p>
<p>One of the most favourite slogans of both the fans and players is, "Who are we? We're The Meat!" (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: "Кто мы? Мясо!", "Kto my? Myaso!")</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rival_teams">Rival teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Spartak_Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Rival teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>At present, Spartak's arch rival is <a href="/wiki/PFC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PFC CSKA Moscow">CSKA Moscow</a>, although this is a relatively-recent rivalry that has only emerged in the last 20 years. Seven of ten matches with the largest audience in Russian Premier League (including top three) were <a href="/wiki/Main_Moscow_derby" title="Main Moscow derby">Spartak-CSKA derbies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Historically, the most celebrated rivalry is with <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Moscow" title="FC Dynamo Moscow">Dynamo Moscow</a>, a fiercely-contested matchup which is <a href="/wiki/Oldest_Russian_derby" title="Oldest Russian derby">Russia's oldest derby</a>. However, this has faded somewhat due to Dynamo's mediocre performances in recent years. Matches against <a href="/wiki/FC_Lokomotiv_Moscow" title="FC Lokomotiv Moscow">Lokomotiv Moscow</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Zenit_Saint_Petersburg" title="FC Zenit Saint Petersburg">Zenit Saint Petersburg</a> attract thousands of people as well, almost always resulting in packed stadia. Upon the collapse of the Soviet Union, Spartak's rivalry with <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv" title="FC Dynamo Kyiv">Dynamo Kyiv</a>, one of the leaders of the USSR championship, was lost. Since Dynamo Kyiv now plays in the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Premier_League" title="Ukrainian Premier League">Ukrainian Premier League</a>, both teams must qualify for <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> tournaments to meet each other.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium">Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Spartak_Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Spartak has never had its own stadium, with the team historically playing in various Moscow stadia throughout its history, even once playing an exhibition match in <a href="/wiki/Red_Square" title="Red Square">Red Square</a>. Currently, the club's home ground is the five-star rated <a href="/wiki/Luzhniki_Stadium" title="Luzhniki Stadium">Luzhniki Stadium</a>.</p>
<p>However, the club's new board has declared that "Spartak will soon play on their <a href="/wiki/Spartak_Moscow_Stadion" title="Spartak Moscow Stadion" class="mw-redirect">own stadium</a>." The Russian government has agreed to give land for the stadium near the <a href="/wiki/Tushino" title="Tushino">Tushino</a> air field. After a set of delays, actual construction begun in December 2010, immediately after Russia obtained the right to host the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>. The stadium was opened on 28 August 2014.</p>

<p>Beginning in 2013, Spartak's farm club, <a href="/wiki/FC_Spartak-2_Moscow" title="FC Spartak-2 Moscow">Spartak-2 Moscow</a>, plays at the professional level in the third-tier <a href="/wiki/Russian_Professional_Football_League" title="Russian Professional Football League">Russian Professional Football League</a>. Spartak's reserve squad previously played professionally as <b>FC Spartak-d Moscow</b> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_Second_League" title="Russian Second League" class="mw-redirect">Russian Second League</a> in 1992–93, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Third_Division" title="Russian Third Division" class="mw-redirect">Russian Third Division</a> in 1994–97) and as <b>FC Spartak-2 Moscow</b> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_Second_Division" title="Russian Second Division" class="mw-redirect">Russian Second Division</a> in 1998–00).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spartak-2">Spartak-2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Spartak_Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Spartak-2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following players are listed by Spartak's website as Spartak-2 players and are registered with the Premier League. They are eligible to play for the first team.</p>
<p><small>Note: Flags indicate national team as defined under <a href="/wiki/FIFA_eligibility_rules" title="FIFA eligibility rules">FIFA eligibility rules</a>. Players may hold more than one non-FIFA nationality.</small></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_players">Notable players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Spartak_Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notable players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Had international caps for their respective countries, or held any club record. Players whose name is listed in <b>bold</b> represented their countries while playing for Spartak. For further list, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_FC_Spartak_Moscow_players" title="List of FC Spartak Moscow players">List of FC Spartak Moscow players</a>.</p>
